Topic: Logic
Context: The basis of life-the main component of protein is an amino acid molecule.It is an organic molecule.Although people have not directly observed amino acid molecules in cosmic space, scientists have used hydrogen, water, oxygen, methane and formaldehyde in the laboratory to simulate the natural conditions of space.Kinds of amino acids.The raw materials used to synthesize amino acids are abundant in interstellar molecules.It is not difficult to imagine that there must also be amino acid molecules in the universe.As long as there is an appropriate environment, they may be transformed into proteins and further develop into organic life.According to this speculation, there are living bodies on other planets than the earth, and may even be living bodies with higher intelligence.
Question: Which of the following is true to best refute the above speculation?
Choices:
  A: There is a huge difference between the process of developing from protein to organic life and the process from organic molecules to protein
  B: Higher intelligence is not only a product of material evolution, but also a product of continuous socialization
  C: In the natural environment, the synthesis of amino acid molecules from existing interstellar molecules is a small probability event
  D: Some interstellar molecules are not found in the Earth â€™s environment, and they are still not available in the laboratory
Response 0:
Thought:
  The speculation is that there may be living bodies on other planets than earth, and they may have higher intelligence.
  We need to select the option that best refutes the speculation.
  Option A talks about differences between two processes, but not about the possibility of life on other planets.
  Option B talks about higher intelligence, but not about the possibility of life on other planets.
  Option D talks about some molecules not being available in the laboratory, but it is not directly related to the possibility of life on other planets.
  Option C talks about the probability of amino acid molecule synthesis in natural environment, and if it's low, it would refute the speculation.
  Therefore, the answer is C: In the natural environment, the synthesis of amino acid molecules from existing interstellar molecules is a small probability event. 
Action: Answer("C")

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 2 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: Placebo effect" refers to the phenomenon of letting patients take fake drugs that have no effect at all without knowing it, but they can get the same or better effects than real drugs.The "placebo effect" has been supported by many clinical studies.One explanation for this phenomenon is that human expectations for the future will change the physiological state of the brain, which in turn will cause physiological changes throughout the body.
Question: The following statements can support the above explanation, except
Choices:
  A: The placebo effect is the result of a combination of factors.
  B: Placebo has no effect on Alzheimer's patients who have lost their expected future abilities.
  C: Some patients do not believe that the treatment will be effective.Although they have been treated normally, their condition has worsened.
  D: Inject the subject with normal saline and make him believe that it is an analgesic.The subject's brain then secretes the analgesic endorphin.
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The explanation given in the context is about expectation of future changes the physiological state of the brain, which in turn will cause physiological changes throughout the body.
  A supports the above explanation as it suggests multiple factors are at play.
  B contradicts the explanation as it suggests loss of expectation does not lead to changes in physiological state.
  C supports the above explanation as it suggests that believing in the treatment contributes positively to the physiological changes.
  D supports the above explanation as it describes how making the subject believe that saline is analgesic can lead to the secretion of endorphins.
  Therefore, the statement that does not support the above explanation is B as it contradicts the explanation.
Action: Answer("B")

  Therefore, the answer is B: Placebo has no effect on Alzheimer's patients who have lost their expected future abilities.

Question: Which of the following best explains the contradictory statement above?
Choices:
  A: The sampling of the survey sample is not random and therefore not representative.
  B: Some respondents later changed their views.
  C: Many investigators believe that the causes of the "September 11" terrorist attacks were not single but compound.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 4 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: There are 6 scholars F, G, J, L, M, and N, who will speak at a logical meeting, and the speeches are arranged in the following order? (1) Each speaker speaks only once, and only once at the same time By.(2) Three speakers speak before lunch, and the other three speak after lunch.(3) G must speak before lunch.(4) Only one speaker is between M and N.(5) F speaks in the first or third place.
Question: If the speeches of M and N are separated by lunch, which of the following lists all speakers that can be arranged between M and N?
Choices:
  A: G, J
  C: F, G, J
  B: J, L
  D: F, G, J, L
Response 0:
Thought:
  M and N are separated by lunch.
  Therefore, M and N should not speak consecutively and should be placed before and after lunch.
  F speaks in the first or third place.
  Therefore, F cannot be between M and N.
  G must speak before lunch and only three speakers speak before lunch.
  Therefore, G cannot be between M and N.
  Only one speaker is between M and N.
  Therefore, either J or L will be between M and N.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  According to the condition (2), there are 3 speakers before lunch and 3 speakers after lunch. Therefore, the only possible sequence of speakers is:
  [G, [ ], [ ], N, M, [ ], [ ]]
  According to the condition (4), M and N must be separated by only one speaker. The only possible sequence is: 
  [G, J, L, N, M, F, [ ]]
  According to the condition (5), F speaks in the first or third place. Only one speaker is empty between F and G. 
  Therefore, the only valid list of speakers between M and N is J and L. 
  The answer is B: J, L.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  We know that G speaks before lunch.
  There are three speakers before lunch and three speakers after lunch.
  F speaks in the first or third place.
  Only one speaker is between M and N, and they are separated by lunch.
  Therefore, M and N must be the last two speakers.
  F speaks in the first or third place, so the three speakers before lunch cannot be F.
  Therefore, F must speak after lunch along with L.
  Thus, the speakers between M and N are G, J.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Thought:
  If M and N are separated by lunch, there are only two possible arrangements:   M is before lunch, and N is after lunch or N is before lunch, and M is after lunch.
  From (4) we know that there is only one speaker (not neither) between M and N.
  If M is before lunch, then the only possible speaker between M and N is G according to (3). If N is before lunch, then the only possible speaker between M and N is J according to (2).
  F must speak in the first or third place according to (5), which has no impact on the relationship between M and N.
  Therefore, the only speakers that can be arranged between M and N are either G or J.
  The answer is A: G, J.

  G _ _ M _ _ N
  F can be the first speaker or the third speaker.
  J and L can take the spaces between M and N.
  Therefore, the possible list of speakers between M and N are J and L.

  And, G and F speak before lunch.
  We know that only one speaker is between M and N.
  Therefore, the only possibility is J and L.
  The answer is B: J, L.

Context: Essayist? Wisdom and cleverness are desirable qualities.However, being smart does not mean that he is very smart, and being smart does not mean that he is very smart.Some of the people I met were smart and some were wise, but no one possessed both qualities.
Question: If the essayist's statement is true, which of the following options cannot be true?
Choices:
  A: No one is smart but no wisdom, and no one is smart but not smart.
  B: Most people are smart and wise.
  C: No one is smart and wise.
  D: Most people are neither smart nor wise.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The essayist states that they have not met any person who is both smart and wise.
  Option A is possible since there can be people who are not smart and not wise.
  Option B cannot be true since the essayist's statement implies that there are no people who possess both qualities.
  Option C is possible since it agrees with the essayist's statement.
  Option D is possible since it includes people who are not smart or wise, which is compatible with the essayist's statement.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Most people are smart and wise.
Action: Answer("B")

Topic: Logic
Context: twenty one.Standard antibiotics usually contain only one active ingredient, while herbal antibacterial drugs contain many.Therefore, herbal medicines are more likely to maintain their effectiveness than standard antibiotics when fighting new resistant bacteria.For the strain, it is difficult to develop resistance to herbal medicines, just as it is difficult for a chef to make a dish that can satisfy the taste of dozens of guests at the same time, and it is much easier to make a dish that meets the taste of one guest.
Question: Which of the following ways of reasoning is most similar to the above argument?
Choices:
  A: If you have a large deposit in the bank, your purchasing power will be strong.If your purchasing power is strong, you will be happy.Therefore, if your bank has a large amount of deposits, you will be happy.
  B: A full-term baby has a certain instinct reaction after birth that will disappear by 2 months.The baby has been 3 months old, and there is this instinctive reaction.Therefore, this baby was not born at full term.
  C: Depending on the size, the supermarket may require 1 to 3 security guards to prevent theft.If any supermarket decides to use 3 security guards, then it must be a big supermarket.
  D: Electric current passes through wires as water flows through pipes.Since a large-diameter pipeline has a larger flow rate than a small-diameter pipeline, a thicker wire has a larger amount of electricity than a thin wire.
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The argument is about the effectiveness of bacterial drugs.
  The argument suggests that herbal medicines are more effective than standard antibiotics in fighting new resistant bacteria.
  This is because herbal medicines contain many active ingredients, making it difficult for bacteria to develop resistance.
  This is compared to standard antibiotics, which contain only one active ingredient.
  The argument uses an analogy of a chef making a dish that can satisfy many guests, which is difficult, compared to making a dish that meets the taste of one guest, which is much easier.
  This analogy suggests that it is difficult for bacteria to develop resistance to herbal medicines because they contain many active ingredients, making it difficult for bacteria to "satisfy" all the active ingredients at the same time.
  The argument is similar in structure to answer choice C.
  Answer choice C also uses a conditional statement and a conclusion.
  The conditional statement suggests that the number of security guards in a supermarket depends on the size of the supermarket.
  The conclusion suggests that if a supermarket uses 3 security guards, then it must be a big supermarket.
  Both arguments use a similar structure of conditional statement and conclusion.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 11 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: An editor is considering the issue of choosing the manuscript for the theoretical version of the newspaper.Six papers from E, F, G, J and K are available.Taking into account the content of the article, the layout of the newspaper and other factors.(1) If paper E is used, then paper F cannot be used but paper K must be used; (2) Paper G or paper H can only be used without paper J.(3) If you don't need thesis G, you don't need thesis K.(4) Essay E is a manuscript requested by a celebrity and cannot be used.
Question: If the above items are true, which of the following items must be true?
Choices:
  A: Paper E is used, but paper H is not used.
  B: Both articles G and H are used.
  C: No paper J, but paper K.
  D: Both G and J articles are unnecessary.
Response 0:
Thought:
- According to (1), E implies not F and K. So, if E is not used, either F or K (or both) must be used.
- According to (2), either G or H can be used without J. So, if G is used, H or K (or both) can be used. If H is used, G cannot be used, and K must be used.
- According to (3), if G is not used, K cannot be used.
- According to (4), E cannot be used.
- From the above deductions:
  - If E is not used, it is possible to use F and K instead.
  - If G is used, K must be used, and J cannot be used. H is optional.
  - If H is used, K must be used. G cannot be used. J is optional.
  - If G is not used, K cannot be used. J is optional.
  - E cannot be used in any case.
- Therefore, the only option that must be true is that there is no paper J and paper K is used.
- The answer is C: No paper J, but paper K. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Article E cannot be used.
  If article E is not used, then article K is not used.
  If article G is used, then article J cannot be used.
  If article G is not used, then article H cannot be used.
  Based on the above, there are two possible scenarios: 
    - Scenario 1: Articles F, G, and K are used, but not articles E, H, or J.
    - Scenario 2: Articles H, K, and either F or G are used, but not articles E or J.
  Therefore, the statement "No paper J, but paper K" must be true. 
  The statement "Paper E is used, but paper H is not used" is false because Paper E cannot be used. 
  The statement "Both articles G and H are used" is not necessarily true, as there are two possible scenarios. 
  The statement "Both G and J articles are unnecessary" is false because at least one of them must be used. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:

  (3) If you don't need thesis G, you don't need thesis K.
  (4) Essay E is a manuscript requested by a celebrity and cannot be used.
  These three statements provide us with a restriction on paper E, F, G, J, and K.
  From statement (1), if paper E is used, then paper F cannot be used but paper K must be used.
  From statement (3), if we don't need G, then we don't need K.
  And from statement (4), E cannot be used.
  Therefore, we can't use E, and if we don't use G, we can't use K.
  It means we need to use G if we want to use K.
  Also, if we use G, then we can't use J.
  So, the only possible option is to use K and not use J.
  And because we can't use F, we have to use H.
  Therefore, the only option that must be true is C: No paper J, but paper K.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 12 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: One of the strictest laws in history to ban smoking, although it has not yet banned people from smoking in their homes, it prohibits people from smoking in all public places and workplaces.If this law is strictly enforced, it will completely protect workers from second-hand smoke.
Question: If which of the following statements is true, the above argument is weakened most effectively?
Choices:
  A: The exhaust of cars from people commuting to work is much more harmful than smoking second-hand smoke.
  B: Persons such as tutors, nurses, hourly workers, etc.all work at the employer â€™s home.
  C: No piece of legislation and its implementation can fully realize the intent of the legislator.
  D: This smoking control law overestimates the dangers of smoking secondhand smoke.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The argument states that the smoking ban in public places will protect workers from second-hand smoking.
  We need to look for a statement that weakens this argument the most.
  A may be irrelevant to the argument.
  B suggests that some people work in employers' homes, which is not relevant to the argument.
  C is a general statement and not a specific counter-argument against the argument.
  D opposes the argument.
  If the smoking control law overestimates the dangers of smoking secondhand smoke, then the argument that the ban will protect workers from the smoke weakens. 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The argument states that the strict smoking ban will protect workers from second-hand smoke.
  To weaken the argument, we need to find a statement that challenges the effectiveness of the strict smoking ban in public places and workplaces.
  Option A presents an alternative harmful factor that is not related to second-hand smoke, so it is not relevant to the argument.
  Option B presents a scenario where workers are working in private residences, so the smoking ban does not apply. However, this does not necessarily weaken the effectiveness of the ban in public places and workplaces.
  Option C is a general statement that applies to all laws and regulations, and it does not undermine the effectiveness of the smoking ban.
  Option D challenges the premise that the dangers of second-hand smoke are as high as the law assumes. If this were true, then the strict smoking ban may not be necessary or effective.
  Therefore, the answer is D: This smoking control law overestimates the dangers of smoking secondhand smoke.

  B: No one can be allowed to stop flying.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 22 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: In a cooking competition, the chef is required to make one hot dish and one cold dish, and the results are evaluated as "top grade", "middle grade", and "bottom grade".If each result of the chef is not lower than that of Chef B, and at least one item is higher than Chef B, it is said that "Chef A is more skilled than Chef B".There are a number of existing chefs, none of them is more skilled than the other, and no two people have the same hot dishes and cold dishes.
Question: How many chefs can meet the above conditions?
Choices:
  A: unconfirmed
  B: 9 people
  C: 6 people
  D: 3 people
Response 0:
Thought:
  Each chef prepares two dishes, one hot dish, and one cold dish. 
  There are no two people have the same hot dishes and cold dishes.
  Therefore, there are 9 different dishes.
  Since none of the chefs are more skilled than each other, each chef should get a different rank.
  If we assume the ranks are top grade, middle grade, and bottom grade, then there are 3 ways to assign the ranks to the 3 chefs.
  Therefore, the number of chefs that can meet the above conditions is 3 x 3 = 9.
  The answer is B: 9 people.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  If we assume there is only one chef, then there is no other chef to compare the skills with, so the condition cannot be satisfied.
  If there are two chefs, and they have the same hot and cold dishes, then no one can be more skilled than the other, so the condition is not satisfied.
  If there are two chefs, and they have different hot and cold dishes, and the result of each chef in both the hot and cold dishes is not lower than the other chef, and at least one dish is higher than the other chef's, then the condition is satisfied. There are C(9,2) = 36 combinations of two dishes from the nine dishes, so there are 36 ways to choose two chefs. However, each combination only satisfies the condition if the two chefs have completely different hot and cold dishes. There are 9*8=72 ways to choose two different dishes from the nine dishes, so there are 72 combinations of two chefs to satisfy the condition. But each combination can be counted twice (for example, if Chef A and Chef B satisfy the condition, then Chef B and Chef A also satisfy the condition), so there are 72/2=36 combinations of two chefs to satisfy the condition.
  If there are three chefs, and they have the same hot and cold dishes, then no one can be more skilled than the other, so the condition is not satisfied.
  If there are three chefs, and they have different hot and cold dishes, then there are C(9,3)=84 combinations of three dishes from the nine dishes, so there are 84 ways to choose three chefs. However, each combination only satisfies the condition if the three chefs have completely different hot and cold dishes. There are 9*8*7=504 ways to choose three different dishes from the nine dishes, so there are 504 combinations of three chefs to satisfy the condition. But each combination can be counted six times (for example, if Chef A, Chef B, and Chef C satisfy the condition, then there are six ways to order them to compare their skills). So there are 504/6=84 combinations of three chefs to satisfy the condition.
  The above analysis shows that there are only 36+84=120 combinations of chefs that satisfy the condition. Since each chef can only be used once in a combination, there can be at most 9+36+84=129 chefs. However, this number is impossible because each chef can only be in C(9,2)=36 combinations, and there are C(129,2)=8256 combinations of two chefs. So at most 8256/36=229 chefs can exist, which is greater than 129. Therefore, the number of chefs that can meet the above conditions is unconfirmed.

When the economy in a region is sluggish, many people are unemployed, so they reduce their living expenses, resulting in more unemployment and worsening the economy.The economy continued to deteriorate, and finally prices fell to the lowest point.Low prices have stimulated people to increase their living consumption, and increased consumption has led to improved economic conditions.Li Ming?   A: After the economic situation improves, the company will hire more people, and many people who are reemployed will buy the goods that have been delayed.

Topic: Logic
Context: A unit arranges for 6 people on duty on the first day, second day, third day of the new year.They are G., H, K, L, P, and S.Two people are required per day.The personnel arrangement must meet the following conditions? (1) L and P must be on duty on the same day.(2) G and H cannot be on duty on the same day.(3) If K is on the first day of duty, then G is on the second day of duty.(4 ) If S is on the third day of duty, then H is on the second day of duty.
Question: If H is on duty the same day before S, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: G on the second day of duty
  B: P on duty in the second day
  C: K on duty in the first day
  D: H on duty at the first day
Response 0:
Thought: 
  If H is on duty the same day before S, then H must be on duty on the second day.
  If H is on duty on the second day, then G cannot be on duty on the second day, because G and H cannot be on duty on the same day.
  Therefore, G must be on duty on the first day.
  If K is on the first day of duty, then G is on the second day of duty.
  Therefore, K cannot be on the first day of duty, because G is already assigned to the second day.
  So, L and P must be on the first day of duty.
  If L and P are on the first day of duty, then H and S must be on the third day of duty because S is after H.
  Therefore, K must be on the second day of duty, because K is the only one left.
  The answer is C: K on duty in the first day.
Action: Answer("C")

  Then, from statement (4), we know that G must be on the first day of duty.

  From statement (3), we know that if K is on the first day of duty, then G is on the second day of duty. 
  However, we already know that G is on the first day of duty, so K cannot be on the first day of duty. 
  From statement (1), we know that L and P must be on duty on the same day, but we don't have enough information to determine which day that is. 
  Therefore, the only option that must be true is A: G on the second day of duty.

Question: Which of the following statements, if true, can reasonably explain the seemingly contradictory phenomenon?
Choices:
  A: Among those who choose to "will invite college students to be nanny", 75% intend to let college students work as tutors or secretaries, and only 25% want college students to do housework.
  B: 62% of the people in the survey indicated that they were only willing to pay a monthly salary of 800 yuan to 1,000 yuan for the college nanny.
  C: Among those who favor college students as nanny, 69% think that doing housekeeping work is good for college students themselves, and only 31% think that college students nanny can provide better housekeeping services.
  D: Among those who do not approve of college students being nanny, 40% believe that students should choose a field related to their major in practice.

  But almost 60% of the respondents said "no" when asked if they would ask college students to be nanny.

  Option C may explain the seemingly contradictory phenomenon.
  If the majority of those who favor college students as nanny think that doing housekeeping work is good for college students themselves, then they may be unwilling to hire college students as nanny to do housekeeping work.
  Therefore, option C is the best answer.

Topic: Logic
Context: There are 7 heart disease patients E, F, G, H, I, J, K to be assigned to 4 doctors for treatment, they are Dr.Zhang, Dr.Li, Dr.Wang and Dr.Liu.Only one doctor is responsible for each patient, and each doctor is responsible for the treatment of up to two patients.Among the patients, J and K are children, and the remaining 5 are adults; E, F, and J are males, and the remaining 4 are females.The following conditions must be met? (1) Dr.Zhang is only responsible for treating male patients.(2) Dr.Li can only be responsible for the treatment of 1 patient.(3) If a doctor is responsible for treating a child patient, then he must be responsible for the treatment of an adult patient of the same sex as the child.
Question: According to the question, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: Dr.Wang is responsible for treating at least one female patient.
  B: Dr.Wang is responsible for treating at least one child patient.
  C: Dr.Liu is responsible for treating at least one male patient.
  D: Dr.Liu is responsible for treating at least one child patient.
Response 0:
Thought:
- There are 2 child patients, J and K.
- If a doctor is responsible for treating a child patient, then he must be responsible for the treatment of an adult patient of the same sex as the child.
- Therefore, there must be at least 2 doctors who are responsible for the treatment of child patients.
- Dr.Li can only be responsible for the treatment of 1 patient.
- Therefore, Dr.Li must be responsible for treating an adult patient.
- From (1) we know that Dr.Zhang is only responsible for treating male patients.
- Therefore, Dr.Zhang must be responsible for treating an adult male patient.
- The remaining 3 doctors (Dr.Wang, Dr.Liu, and one more doctor) must be responsible for treating the remaining 4 patients (3 adult female patients and 1 child male patient).
- From (3), the doctor who is responsible for treating the child male patient must also be responsible for treating an adult male patient.
- Therefore, Dr.Wang must be responsible for treating an adult female patient and the child male patient, and Dr.Liu must be responsible for treating the remaining 2 adult female patients.
- Therefore, Dr.Wang is responsible for treating at least one female patient, but not necessarily more than one.
- Dr.Wang is responsible for treating one child patient, but not necessarily more than one.
- Dr.Liu is responsible for treating at least one male patient, but not necessarily more than one.
- Therefore, the answer is none of the above.

Thought:

(1) The warehouse number for storing G is larger than the warehouse number for storing L.(2) The warehouse number storing L is larger than the warehouse number storing T.(3) The warehouse number storing P is larger than the warehouse number storing F.(4) The warehouse storing T is next to the warehouse storing P.
Question: If there is exactly one warehouse between the warehouse where M is stored and the warehouse where G is stored, how many kinds of goods are stored in the warehouse?
Choices:
  A: 2 rooms
  B: 3 rooms
  C: 4
  D: 5 rooms

Context: A company has six general manager assistants F, G, H, I, M and P, and three departments, each of which is in charge of three general manager assistants.Each assistant general manager is in charge of at least one department.The following conditions must be met? (1) There is only one assistant to the general manager in charge of three departments at the same time.(2) F and G are not in charge of the same department.(3) H and I are not in charge of the same department.
Question: If F and M are not in charge of the same department, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: F and H are in charge of the same department.
  B: F and I are in charge of the same department.
  C: I and P are in charge of the same department.
  D: M and G are in charge of the same department.
Response 0:

  If F and I are in charge of the same department, then H and G will be in charge of the same department, which is not violating any condition.
  If I and P are in charge of the same department, then H and G will be in charge of the same department, which is not violating any condition.
  If M and G are in charge of the same department, then F, H, and I will be in charge of the same department, which violates (1).
  Therefore, the answer is either B or C.

  A: Many disputes have been resolved without a mediator.
  B: Those who filed prosecutions are unreasonable and will refuse to listen to the mediator â€™s opinion.

  Option A does not criticize the proposal enough.
  Option B is a criticism of the defendants, not the proposal.

Context: The lower the credit rating of the borrower, the higher the cost of borrowing and the higher the rate of return for the creditor.On August 5, 2011, S & P downgraded the US sovereign credit rating from AAA to AA +.According to common sense, investors should reduce their holdings of U.S.Treasury bonds when they are in a safe haven, thereby pushing their prices down and yields rising.However, on August 8, the price of US Treasury bonds rose, and the yield fell, and the yield of the latest 10-year US Treasury bond fell to 2.34%, a new low this year.
Question: If any of the following statements are true, can we best explain the above-mentioned violation of common sense?
Choices:
  A: On the evening of August 5, the US Treasury responded that S & P had a $ 2 trillion error in its rating calculations.
  B: Compared with the bonds of the European Union, Japan and other countries, US Treasuries are still relatively safe and liquid investment products.
  C: After the US sovereign credit rating was lowered, Russia began to reduce its holdings of US Treasury bonds, while China still increased its holdings of US Treasury bonds.
  D: In order to break the monopoly of three US rating agencies including S & P, the EU plans to establish a European credit rating agency.

  Option D is not relevant to the question.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 85 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: There are two types of horror stories? one type of experiments depicting mad scientists, and one type of fierce monsters.In the horror story about monsters, monsters symbolize the chaos of the hero's psychology.The horror stories about crazy scientists typically express the author's feelings? scientific knowledge alone is not enough to guide human exploration activities.Despite these differences, these two types of horror stories have the following common characteristics? they describe phenomena that violate the laws of nature? they both want to make the reader feel fear.
Question: If the above statement is true, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: All descriptions of monsters describe phenomena that violate the laws of nature.
  B: Some stories that use symbolic techniques describe phenomena that violate the laws of nature.
  C: Most of the stories about crazy scientists express the author's anti-scientific point of view.
  D: Any kind of horror stories are described, psychologically chaotic characters.
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The statement mentions that horror stories about monsters describe the chaos of the hero's psychology, and horror stories about mad scientists express the author's feelings that scientific knowledge alone is not enough to guide human exploration activities. 
  The statement also mentions that both types of horror stories describe phenomena that violate the laws of nature and aim to make the reader feel fear. 
  Choice A is not necessarily true because it only applies to descriptions of monsters, not all horror stories. 
  Choice B can be inferred from the statement because it mentions that both types of horror stories describe phenomena that violate the laws of nature. 
  Choice C is not supported by the statement because it only mentions that horror stories about mad scientists express the author's feelings about scientific knowledge, not necessarily anti-scientific views. 
  Choice D is not necessarily true because it only applies to horror stories with psychologically chaotic characters. 
  Therefore, the answer is B: Some stories that use symbolic techniques describe phenomena that violate the laws of nature. 
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The statement says that both horror stories describe phenomena that violate the laws of nature and want to make the reader feel fear.
  It also says that monsters symbolize the chaos of the hero's psychology and stories about crazy scientists express the author's feelings that scientific knowledge is not enough to guide human exploration activities.
  There is no mention of all descriptions of monsters or any particular percentage of stories about crazy scientists.
  Therefore, the answer must be related to the description of phenomena that violate the laws of nature.
  According to the statement, both types of horror stories describe such phenomena, so it must be true for both types.
  It is not limited to one type or the other.
  Therefore, the answer is A: All descriptions of monsters describe phenomena that violate the laws of nature.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 90 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: Homo erectus originated in Africa about 2 million years ago and spread to Eurasia; modern people appeared about 200,000 years ago.Both human fossils are distributed in China.For example, the "Beijing people" unearthed in the ancient stratum of Zhoukoudian, Beijing belonged to Homo erectus; the "shandingdong people" in the stratum of the previous year belonged to modern people.A study of the contemporary Chinese population found that the Y chromosome inherited from the paternal lineage originated in Africa and originated in 8.9 10,000 years to 35,000 years ago; the mitochondrial DNA inherited from the maternal line originated in Africa, with a time of origin within 100,000 years; no genetic component of H.erectus was detected
Question: If the above statement is true, which hypothesis is best supported?
Choices:
  A: The descendants of "Beijing people" may be extinct.The ancestors of Chinese contemporary people came to Asia from Africa about 100,000 years ago
  B: Chinese Homo erectus and modern people are from the African continent, and their hybrid descendants are the ancestors of contemporary Chinese
  C: The "Stop Cave Man" in Zhoukoudian, Beijing evolved from "Beijing People"
  D: Contemporary Chinese are descendants of Homo erectus that spread from Africa to Eurasia 2 million years ago
Response 0:
Thought:
  The statement mentions that both Homo erectus and modern people fossils are distributed in China. However, no genetic component of Homo erectus was detected from the contemporary Chinese population.
  The study found that the Y chromosome and mitochondrial DNA inherited from the paternal and maternal lineage originated in Africa, but the time of origin is different. The Y chromosome originated in 8.9 10,000 years to 35,000 years ago, while the mitochondrial DNA's time of origin is within 100,000 years.
  Therefore, the hypothesis that best supported by the above statement is that Chinese Homo erectus and modern people are from the African continent, and their hybrid descendants are the ancestors of contemporary Chinese.
  The answer is B: Chinese Homo erectus and modern people are from the African continent, and their hybrid descendants are the ancestors of contemporary Chinese.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The statement mentions that the Homo erectus originated in Africa and spread to Eurasia, and the modern people appeared about 200,000 years ago.
  Both Homo erectus and modern people fossils are found in China.
  The genetic study shows that the Y chromosome inherited from the paternal lineage originated in Africa and originated in 8.9 10,000 years to 35,000 years ago, and the mitochondrial DNA inherited from the maternal line originated in Africa and is within 100,000 years.
  No genetic component of H. erectus was detected.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: Crimes involving the use of firearms are more likely to lead to murder than other types of crimes.However, most crimes involving the use of firearms did not result in homicides.Therefore, there is no need to distinguish the illegal use of firearms as a serious criminal offense in the criminal law from other criminal offenses.
Question: The logic loophole in the above argument is most similar to the following one?
Choices:
  A: Obese people are more likely to suffer from heart disease than people with normal weight.However, obese people make up a very small percentage of our population.Therefore, in our country, there is no need for the medical and health community to emphasize the risk of heart disease.
  B: Unchecked sex is more likely to be infected with AIDS than checkpoint.However, among people with unchecked sex, only a small percentage of people are infected with AIDS.Therefore, there is no need to emphasize the harm of unchecked sex in the propaganda of AIDS prevention.
  C: The prevailing view is that smoking is more likely to cause lung cancer than not smoking.However, in some countries, the proportion of people with lung cancer who have a history of smoking is not higher than the proportion of the total population who have a history of smoking.Therefore, the above popular opinion is likely to be a prejudice.
  D: High-income people are more capable of enjoying life than low-income people.But there are many high-income earners who claim to be unhappy.Therefore, those who pursue a happy life need not pay attention to the level of income.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The argument concludes that there is no need to treat the illegal use of firearms as a serious criminal offense.
  However, the argument does not consider that even if most crimes involving firearms did not result in homicides, they still pose a serious threat to public safety.
  Therefore, the loophole in the argument is that it fails to acknowledge the potential harm of non-lethal crimes involving firearms.
  Choice A is similar because it also fails to consider the potential harm of heart disease in people who are not obese.
  Choice B is not similar because it acknowledges the harm of unchecked sex and only questions the extent of the harm.
  Choice C is not similar because it questions the validity of a popular opinion rather than the potential harm of an action.
  Choice D is not similar because it undermines the importance of income for a happy life, which is not relevant to the argument.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The argument presents a premise that crimes involving the use of firearms are more likely to lead to murder than other types of crimes.
  The argument also presents a premise that most crimes involving the use of firearms did not result in homicides.
  The conclusion is that there is no need to distinguish the illegal use of firearms as a serious criminal offense in the criminal law from other criminal offenses.
  The conclusion does not logically follow the premises because although most crimes involving firearms do not lead to homicides, the remaining percentage of crimes that do lead to homicides is significant enough to warrant distinguishing the illegal use of firearms as a serious criminal offense.
  The logic loophole in the argument is most similar to the following statement: 
  "Obese people make up a very small percentage of our population.Therefore, in our country, there is no need for the medical and health community to emphasize the risk of heart disease."
